  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5f41804a-70ba-47d8-bce4-20e0e7d07dab'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer15495758905931104113">Boston private detectives Patrick Kenzie and Angela Gennaro are hired to find four-year-old Amanda McCready, abducted from her bed on a warm, summer night. They meet her stoned-out, strangely apathetic mother, her loving aunt and uncle, the mother's dangerous, drug-addled friends, and two cops who've found so many abused or dead children they may be too far over the edge t</span>
  <span id="freeText15495758905931104113" style="display:none">Boston private detectives Patrick Kenzie and Angela Gennaro are hired to find four-year-old Amanda McCready, abducted from her bed on a warm, summer night. They meet her stoned-out, strangely apathetic mother, her loving aunt and uncle, the mother's dangerous, drug-addled friends, and two cops who've found so many abused or dead children they may be too far over the edge to come back. Despite enormous public attention, rabid news coverage, and dogged police work, the investigation repeatedly hits a brick wall. Led into a world of drug dealers, child molesters, and merciless executioners, Patrick and Angie are soon forced to face not only the horrors adults can perpetrate on innocents but also their own conflicted feelings about what is best, and worst, when it comes to raising children. And as the Indian summer fades and the autumn chill deepens, Amanda McCready stays gone, banished so completely that she seems never to have existed.<p><b>Then another child disappears. . . . </b>Dennis Lehane takes you into a world of triple crosses, elaborate lies, and shrouded motives, where the villains may be more moral than the victims, the missing should possibly stay missing, and those who go looking for them may not come back alive.</p><p>Settle in and turn off the phone. From its haunting opening to its shocking climax, <i>Gone, Baby, Gone</i> is certain to be one of the most thrilling, talked-about suspense novels you read this year.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="15495758905931104113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/5460575-gina"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1524163626i/5460575._UX100_CR0,16,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/5460575-gina">Gina</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">OMG, yes this movie is excellent! It is one of the best adaptations from page to screen. It manages to capture everything in the book. You will easily<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">OMG, yes this movie is excellent! It is one of the best adaptations from page to screen. It manages to capture everything in the book. You will easily and immediately connect with the characters and storyline. It is gritty crime drama that the director managed to bring to life and not stray from all of the nitty-gritty details in the book that makes this such a good book to read in the first place. So yes, the movie is awesome and definitely worth your time. I highly recommend it!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

  <span id="freeText17086806016816072845" style="display:none"><b>Each day in this country, twenty-three hundred children are reported missing.</b><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/wetj5LH" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441552844ra/16122566.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Kenzie and Angie don't really want to take this case. A missing four year old girl that was taken from her home, while her drugged out mom is supposedly next door at her friend's house watching tv. The mom did not even lock the door. She was in such a hurry that she just left it open. With her child inside.<br> <b>I didn't want to find Amanda McCready. I wanted someone else to.<br>But maybe because I'd become as caught up in this case over the last few days as the rest of the city, or maybe because it had happened here in my neighborhood, or maybe just because "four-year-old" and "missing" aren't words that should go together in the same sentence.</b><br><br>They do end up taking the case and team up with a couple of cops that are on the case. Their old classmate Cheese may factor into the child's disappearance. A drug deal gone bad where money is taken and the child suffers the consequences? <br><a href="http://imgur.com/Idd0mPd" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441552844ra/16122569.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Or is there more to the story? So many twists and turns in this book. Then just when I thought I had somewhat figured it out I got slammed against the wall. <br>This book makes you question right and wrongs in the world. Should things be so black and white? I don't know the answers to these questions and Dennis Lehane I sorta hate you for putting all this in my head. <br><br>I just don't have any more words for this book. I was just going to throw up five stars and walk away. Just read this series. Hug your kids. <br><a href="http://imgur.com/uVMcTJ9" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_6595662" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6595662" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6595662?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=detectives">detectives</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6595662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14231935601270094748">And then depression set in….<br/><br/>This book wrecked me the first time I read it. It was almost like having post traumatic stress syndrome. I found myself staring blankly at the walls for days after I finished it the first time. I felt like calling my sister and telling her to keep my young niece locked in the house until she was at least 25. I remember meeting a friend for beers shortly after I finished it, and that he asked me what was wrong. When I tried to explain, he was skeptical. “You’re really </span>
  <span id="freeText14231935601270094748" style="display:none">And then depression set in….<br /><br />This book wrecked me the first time I read it. It was almost like having post traumatic stress syndrome. I found myself staring blankly at the walls for days after I finished it the first time. I felt like calling my sister and telling her to keep my young niece locked in the house until she was at least 25. I remember meeting a friend for beers shortly after I finished it, and that he asked me what was wrong. When I tried to explain, he was skeptical. “You’re really this bummed over a book?” And yes, I was that bummed over a book.<br /><br />Patrick Kenzie and Angie Gennaro have had enough of the crazy-ass violence that has surrounded them for three novels. They still run their detective agency, but they’re strictly doing routine jobs with no chance of anyone getting hurt. They’re also finally relatively happy with their lives.<br /><br />That changes when they get hired to look for Amanda McCready, a 4 year old girl who has been missing for days. The cops and media are all over it, but Amanda’s aunt and uncle want Patrick and Angie to join the search. The detectives are reluctant, partly because they don’t think that they can do anything that the cops aren’t doing already, and partly because neither of them is anxious to sign on for what is almost surely going to be a case that ends badly. However, the aunt’s desperate request for help gets the better of them. By the end of it all, they’ll really wish they would have just gone on vacation.<br /><br />At this point, you’re probably thinking, “Kemper, you dumb bastard. You read a book about a child abduction by Dennis Lehane, a guy you knew wasn’t exactly Mr. Giggles. Were you really expecting a happy ending?”<br /><br />Yes, I knew it was probably going to be a depressing story, but while I had braced myself for all kinds of terrible things happening to kids (and terrible things do happen), I wasn’t ready for the more banal cruelty and neglect that Lehane sprinkled the book with in regards to how some people treat their children.<br /><br />Amanda’s mother, Helene, is a barfly and small-time doper who doesn’t do anything really bad enough to technically qualify as abuse, but Amanda was usually left to entertain herself in front of the TV. It’s the tiny details that are heartbreaking like when Patrick checks out Amanda’s room and finds a mattress on the floor, few toys, and no books of any kind, not even coloring books. Or when they talk to the people on Amanda’s t-ball team and everyone notes how she’s the quietest kid around who acts like she’s used to being ignored. You’d have to be one cold bastard not to be saddened by it.<br /><br />This is one of the best crime novels I’ve read. Maybe even the best. But you won’t be skipping down the street and whistling any time soon after you read it.<br /><br />**A Few Thoughts on the Movie Version**<br /><br />I was not a fan of Ben Affleck. I thought he was a complete goober, and that Matt Damon must have wrote most of <i>Good Will Hunting</i> because I couldn’t imagine that Ben could read, let alone write anything. When I heard that he was going to be one of the people writing the adapted screenplay and directing the movie version of one of my favorite books, they probably heard my screams of outrage in Hollywood. When he cast his brother Casey as Patrick, I exhausted my extensive vocabulary of profanity and swore I’d never see the movie.<br /><br />Wow. I was definitely wrong on that one. The movie version is not only one of the best crime novel adaptations I’ve seen, it’s just an incredibly good movie, period. (And Ben Affleck’s recent adaptation of another book <i>The Town</i> is also a very good flick so the guy has some very real skills.)<br /><br />What surprised me most is that Affleck made a couple of very smart changes from the book to the movie. He revised Patrick and Angie from veteran smart-ass gun fighting private detectives to a couple of kids who mostly track down people skipping out on bills. That allowed him to introduce the audience to them, and really gave weight to the idea that these were two characters in way over their heads.<br /><br />Affleck also tightened up the story to the point that I’d almost call it an improvement over the book’s plot. That’s incredibly rare. My only complaints are that Angie didn’t come across as Angie-like in the film version (although she still gets one of her best Big Damn Hero moments in the film), and that Bubba has a much smaller role. Plus, Bubba is portrayed more as just a bad-ass street guy rather than the one-man army he is in the book, but again, it works perfectly with the way Affleck chose to tell the story. <br /><br />Now that he’s adapted two crime novels into top-notch movies, I’m ready to start my own chapter of the Ben Affleck fan club. Just as long as he doesn’t do any more Michael Bay movies. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14231935601270094748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6610423-gone-baby-gone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=1990-99">1990-99</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1996090564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9799249200783362407">four year old Amanda walked out of her house in the middle of night while her mother was at neighbors watching TV, and no one heard about her even after days of search. Everything came to a dead end. Amanda's aunt request Petrik and Angie to look for the child. Patrick and Angie found a big clue about the girl's disappearance but things instead of solving gets messier and scarier. <br/><br/>Lehane wrote an exceptional story here about kidnapping, drugs, abuse, and pain. Writing is flawless and gives chill</span>
  <span id="freeText9799249200783362407" style="display:none">four year old Amanda walked out of her house in the middle of night while her mother was at neighbors watching TV, and no one heard about her even after days of search. Everything came to a dead end. Amanda's aunt request Petrik and Angie to look for the child. Patrick and Angie found a big clue about the girl's disappearance but things instead of solving gets messier and scarier. <br /><br />Lehane wrote an exceptional story here about kidnapping, drugs, abuse, and pain. Writing is flawless and gives chills to the readers with almost real description of crime scenes. I found third book in the series to be average but Lehane bounced back superbly and gave us this tightly knit thriller.<br /><br />After completing a book in this series I say to myself, "now you know these two like the back of your hand." but Lehane always proves me wrong and showed me a new side of Patrick and Angie, it's like he is peeling layer after layer in each book. Don't know what I will get after the final book.<br /><br />A dark yet moving read which tells us how unpredictably dangerous people around us can be. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9799249200783362407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7940642392062533213"><b>Posted at <a href='http://www.shelfinflicted.com/2014/05/gone-baby-gone.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shelf Inflicted</a> </b><br/><br/>I knew this was going to be a very dark story. After reading the very disturbing <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122044329' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darkness, Take My Hand</a>, about a vicious and sadistic serial killer who knew no limits when it came to human depravity, I didn’t imagine it could get much worse. I was wrong.<br/><br/>Though Patrick and Angie are tired of the violence and inhumanity that plagued their earlier cases, they agree to accept this latest case of a four-year-old girl who was abducted from her bed. Amanda’s mom, Helene, who i</span>
  <span id="freeText7940642392062533213" style="display:none"><b>Posted at <a href="http://www.shelfinflicted.com/2014/05/gone-baby-gone.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelf Inflicted</a> </b><br /><br />I knew this was going to be a very dark story. After reading the very disturbing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122044329" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkness, Take My Hand</a>, about a vicious and sadistic serial killer who knew no limits when it came to human depravity, I didn’t imagine it could get much worse. I was wrong.<br /><br />Though Patrick and Angie are tired of the violence and inhumanity that plagued their earlier cases, they agree to accept this latest case of a four-year-old girl who was abducted from her bed. Amanda’s mom, Helene, who is far from the perfect parent, uses drugs, drinks, and is addicted to TV. Amanda has a loving aunt and uncle who desperately want her to be found. <br /><br />Patrick and Angie realize that a child’s disappearance must be solved quickly, or it will never be. With the help of two detectives in the Boston Police Department who believe in their own brand of justice, the denizens of their rough Dorchester neighborhood, and of course, Bubba, Patrick and Angie plunge headlong into one of their most difficult, complex, and emotional cases, confronting bad parenting, child abuse, pedophilia, and murder. They learn about themselves and each other, and discover that life and justice are not always black and white. <br /><br />I had a difficult time putting the book down and enjoyed the growth of Angie and Patrick’s relationship, their feelings about children, and the questionable characters with good intentions. The story left me shaken and numb and thinking about it for days. <br /><br />It was a great movie too!</span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061374197" href="/book/show/1245520.Gone_Baby_Gone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12618229-jeff?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12618229-jeff?shelf=thrillers-suspense-spys">thrillers-suspense-spys</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer742720293" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7393136604905522958"><i>“Hello, darkness my old friend…”</i><br/><br/>Having read <b>The Grapes of Wrath</b> earlier this year, I didn’t think another book could top it for sheer despair. Was I ever wrong. It’s as if at the end of the book the Joad’s drove their truck to the local abattoir and let loose on their frustrations.<br/><br/>The book centers on an abduction of a four year old and the involvement of Dennis Lehane’s private investigator duo, Kenzie and Gennaro, in the attempt to recover the child. It’s a journey that takes the reader straigh</span>
  <span id="freeText7393136604905522958" style="display:none"><i>“Hello, darkness my old friend…”</i><br /><br />Having read <b>The Grapes of Wrath</b> earlier this year, I didn’t think another book could top it for sheer despair. Was I ever wrong. It’s as if at the end of the book the Joad’s drove their truck to the local abattoir and let loose on their frustrations.<br /><br />The book centers on an abduction of a four year old and the involvement of Dennis Lehane’s private investigator duo, Kenzie and Gennaro, in the attempt to recover the child. It’s a journey that takes the reader straight down the dark coal shoot into the blackest abyss. What you find there are the baser and crueler elements of what one human can inflict upon another. <br /><br />Reading this brought to mind James Ellroy. Whereas Ellroy’s noir careens into the grotesque, Lehane’s feels like a rasp; uncomfortably, repeatedly going over your emotions till they're raw. There’s no reprieve from the hopelessness and despondency; no island of joy to cradle in, no pause for a gulp of fresh, sweet air.<br /><br />A powerful and moving glimpse into the bleakness of the human condition.<br /><br />I want to thank my friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/722942670?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Kelly</a> for buddy reading this with me. Her daily status updates kept it light.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7393136604905522958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13224620098790179992">5 STARS<br/><br/>This is a brilliant book. <br/>I’ve read most of his published work and I’m a huge fan, especially the Kenzie and Gennaro series.<br/>Lehane has a gift as a writer – his character development is probably the best in the business. By the end of his novels, you feel like you know the main characters as if they are a part of your family. You genuinely care and – in this case, especially – you will feel things deeply.<br/><br/>***POSSIBLE SPOILER, BUT PROBABLY NOT***<br/><br/>I’m not going to lie, it’s difficult to digest</span>
  <span id="freeText13224620098790179992" style="display:none">5 STARS<br /><br />This is a brilliant book. <br />I’ve read most of his published work and I’m a huge fan, especially the Kenzie and Gennaro series.<br />Lehane has a gift as a writer – his character development is probably the best in the business. By the end of his novels, you feel like you know the main characters as if they are a part of your family. You genuinely care and – in this case, especially – you will feel things deeply.<br /><br />***POSSIBLE SPOILER, BUT PROBABLY NOT***<br /><br />I’m not going to lie, it’s difficult to digest at the end, because you will have to ask yourself this question:<br />When is doing the right thing the wrong thing to do?<br /><br />In terms of quality, I will put this story right up there with Mystic River as his best work.</span>

<div id="review_722942670" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/722942670" />
    <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar"><img alt="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530646317p2/11183856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/722942670?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061336218" href="/book/show/16973.Gone_Baby_Gone">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer722942670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4496770212487982992">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i> “Even if MY world is okay, THE world is still a pile of evil shit.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431702867ra/14860972.gif' alt='Houston commercial photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>(Wrong movie - spot-on quote. Also, doesn’t Matt Damon have the most punchable face in all the world? The correct answer is yes. Yes he does.)<br/><br/>This was a buddy read with my pal <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/742720293' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Jeff</a>, but I can’t wait any longer for his slow ass to finish so my review is going up now ; )<br/><br/>In all seriousness, words can’t express how thankful I am that I buddied up with The Jeff </span>
  <span id="freeText4496770212487982992" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><b>
  <i> “Even if MY world is okay, THE world is still a pile of evil shit.”</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431702867ra/14860972.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>(Wrong movie - spot-on quote. Also, doesn’t Matt Damon have the most punchable face in all the world? The correct answer is yes. Yes he does.)<br><br>This was a buddy read with my pal <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/742720293" rel="nofollow noopener">The Jeff</a>, but I can’t wait any longer for his slow ass to finish so my review is going up now ; )<br><br>In all seriousness, words can’t express how thankful I am that I buddied up with The Jeff for this one. Let’s just say I wasn’t in a real good place this past week so there was no way I could have made it through without adding some levity via status updates with my pal.<br><br><i>Gone Baby Gone</i> is the fourth installment in the Kenzie &amp; Gennaro series and covers the investigation of a 4-year old little girl who has gone missing in Dorchester. Man this book was dark. It’s a story that won’t just break your heart, it might break your entire <i>being</i>. It will most definitely tear your blood pumper into ten thousand pieces, douse those pieces with gasoline, and light the match. <br><br>I’ve never read a book where I already knew the whodunit before even beginning. However, since <i>Gone Baby Gone</i> was a feature film starring the incomparable Morgan Freeman about 8 or so years ago, I was already familiar with the story. That being said, Lehane’s writing is so stellar that even though I totally knew how things would play out I still found myself . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431702867ra/14860973.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>and questioning whether my memory was correct.<br><br>Speaking of the writing . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“Nothing is louder than the silence of the missing child. It’s a silence that’s two and a half to three feet tall, and you feel it at your hip and hear it rising up from the floorboards, shouting to you from corners and crevices and the emotionless face of a doll left on the floor by the bed. It’s a silence that’s different from the one left at funerals and wakes. The silence of the dead carries with it a sense of finality; it’s a silence you know you must get used to. But the silence of a missing child is not something you want to get used to; you refuse to accept it, and so it screams at you. <br><br>The silence of the dead says, Goodbye.<br><br>The silence of the missing says, Find me.”</i>
</b><br><br>Excuse me for a second . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431702867ra/14860974.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>With regard to the movie version if you’ve not yet seen it, let me tell you it’s one of the best adaptations from page to screen I’ve seen (even the miscasting of certain characters worked well). And while I don’t find Battfleck as punchable as Matt Damon, I’m not a huge fan of his acting <s>in</s>ability. However, as a director of a gritty crime drama set in Southie???? Amazing. The film also happens to feature one of the most quotable quotes in the history of movies and one that I use around my house on the regular . . . .<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431702867ra/14860975.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>(Don’t you wish you were married to me? Yeah, Jeff does too.)<br><br>I’m obviously not going to tell you who the bad guy is, any twists and turns, or how things play out. All I’m going to say is some people shouldn’t ever be allowed to birth children . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431702867ra/14860976.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Drugs are bad mmmmm’kay . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431702867ra/14860977.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Don’t <b>EVER</b> f*&amp;^ around with people named things like “Cheese” . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431702867ra/14860978.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And when things seem a little far-fetched or too hinky, just go with it and be prepared for a read that makes you question <s>everything</s> a lot of the opinions you hold about what is right and what is wrong. Also be prepared to . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431702867ra/14860979.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_472845407" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/472845407" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/472845407?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=crime-and-mystery">crime-and-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer472845407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9398679551924153501">When a little girl goes missing and her mother's brother and sister-in-law hire them to find her, Patrick and Angela reluctantly accept. Their investigation drags them through a labyrinth of lies, one they will not emerge from unscathed...<br/><br/>Sweet zombie Jesus this is some good shit! I think Lehane might be the newest member of my crime fiction Holy Trinity with Lawrence Block and Richard Stark. Here's how it all went down.<br/><br/>After the events of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/425124.Sacred__Kenzie___Gennaro__3_' title='Sacred (Kenzie & Gennaro #3) by Dennis Lehane' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sacred</a>, the previous book in the series, Patrick and Ang</span>
  <span id="freeText9398679551924153501" style="display:none">When a little girl goes missing and her mother's brother and sister-in-law hire them to find her, Patrick and Angela reluctantly accept. Their investigation drags them through a labyrinth of lies, one they will not emerge from unscathed...<br /><br />Sweet zombie Jesus this is some good shit! I think Lehane might be the newest member of my crime fiction Holy Trinity with Lawrence Block and Richard Stark. Here's how it all went down.<br /><br />After the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/425124.Sacred__Kenzie___Gennaro__3_" title="Sacred (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro #3) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Sacred</a>, the previous book in the series, Patrick and Angela have more or less shacked up and have started bringing in big money. When Amanda McCready's family hires them, they take the case for the good of the child. I thought I had an idea where the case would go but it turned out I was way off. Gone, Baby, Gone was like walking down the sidewalk to get the mail and somehow ending up in Paraguay.<br /><br />Gone, Baby, Gone is the most powerful Lehane book I've read yet. I thought I was desensitized to crimes against children from reading the Andrew Vachss Burke books but I was wrong. Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/405390-kemper" rel="nofollow noopener">Mrs. Kemper's husband </a> and I were discussing while I was reading, Angela and Patrick are much better people than Burke so the pieces of excrement they go up against while looking for a missing child seem that much more vile.<br /><br />Lehane's strength is in his characters and he writes them very well. Patrick and Angela are the same people I've grown to know and love over the past few books. I felt like they dragged me to hell with them over the course of the investigation. Broussard and Poole drove the story forward and were likeable guys. I alternated feeling contempt and pity for Amanda's mother, Helene. Even Cheese was a well-realized character. Once things went pear-shaped, I couldn't believe Lehane had pulled the wool over my eyes so thoroughly, only to yank the rug out from under me so hard that I banged my head on the radiator.<br /><br />I really can't say much more without giving away too much of the plot. Lehane made a believer out of me on this one. Five easy stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9398679551924153501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2030799442" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2030799442" />
    <a title="William" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36549125-william"><img alt="William" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593268986p2/36549125.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2030799442?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="William" class="user" itemprop="url" name="William" href="/user/show/36549125-william">William</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6610423-gone-baby-gone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36549125-william?shelf=extraordinary-books">extraordinary-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2030799442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11935343562769098237">Five stars, and more. <br/><br/><b>A Masterpiece of crime noir, complex and thrilling, with a difficult and courageous ending.</b><br/><br/><i> As usual with my reviews, please first read the publisher’s blurb/summary of the book so that I don't have to repeat the basic plot. </i> <br/><br/>I am struck by how similar Lehane’s writing is to Robert B. Parker’s, and yet how different the feeling is. In Lehane, the sense of pain and loss, especially of lost childhood friends, weighs heavily upon Patrick and Angie, and through them, on us. <br/><br/>I’m</span>
  <span id="freeText11935343562769098237" style="display:none">Five stars, and more. <br><br><b>A Masterpiece of crime noir, complex and thrilling, with a difficult and courageous ending.</b><br><br><i> As usual with my reviews, please first read the publisher’s blurb/summary of the book so that I don't have to repeat the basic plot. </i> <br><br>I am struck by how similar Lehane’s writing is to Robert B. Parker’s, and yet how different the feeling is. In Lehane, the sense of pain and loss, especially of lost childhood friends, weighs heavily upon Patrick and Angie, and through them, on us. <br><br>I’m also very impressed with how much Lehane’s prose increases in power and control with every book. This is book #4 and he’s already a giant. Wow.<br><br>2% ... This is the introduction to a much, much deeper novel. This is the surface, the emotions we all share, but it's only the beginning of where Lehane wants to go.<br><i>“Amanda McCready had been missing for at least sixty hours by this point, maybe as long as seventy, and I didn’t want to find her stuffed in a Dumpster somewhere, her hair matted with blood. I didn’t want to find her six months down the road, vacant-eyed and used up by some freak with a video camera and a mailing list of pedophiles. I didn’t want to look in a four-year-old’s eyes and see the death of everything that had been pure in her.”</i><br><br>5% ... Wow... Down we go, in Lehane's assured hands...<br><i>“When a child disappears, the space she’d occupied is immediately filled with dozens of people. And these people—relatives, friends, police officers, reporters from both TV and print—create a lot of energy and noise, a sense of communal intensity, of fierce and shared dedication to a task. <br><br>“But amid all that noise, nothing is louder than the silence of the missing child. It’s a silence that’s two and a half to three feet tall, and you feel it at your hip and hear it rising up from the floorboards, shouting to you from corners and crevices and the emotionless face of a doll left on the floor by the bed. <br><br>“It’s a silence that’s different from the one left at funerals and wakes. The silence of the dead carries with it a sense of finality; it’s a silence you know you must get used to. But the silence of a missing child is not something you want to get used to; you refuse to accept it, and so it screams at you.<br><br>“The silence of the dead says, Goodbye. <br><br>“The silence of the missing says, Find me.”</i><br><br>7% ... Deeper still. If you have kids, you know this already... Here is Doyle speaking:<br><i>“But for two minutes, while we’re standing in this Dunkin’ Donuts waiting for our coffee, I look at Tricia and she looks at me and both of us, without saying a word, know that if Shannon is dead, we’re dead, too. Our marriage—over. Our happiness—over. Our lives would be one long road of pain. Nothing else, really. Everything good and hopeful, everything we lived for, really, would die with our daughter.”</i><br><br>8% ... Do you think Trump read this? Lehane wrote it in 1998....<br><i>“She was lonely; there were no good men left; they needed to put a fence up around Mexico to keep out all those Mexicans who were apparently stealing jobs up here in Boston. She was sure there was a liberal agenda to corrupt every decent American but she couldn’t articulate what that agenda was, only that it affected her ability to be happy and it was determined to keep blacks on welfare. Sure, she was on welfare herself, but she’d been trying hard these last seven years to get off.”</i><br><br>18% ... Wow. Very powerful and dark scene begins here. Patrick lost in the terrors of his past. A page or two of true brilliance from Lehane:<br><i>“... every time I looked at one of the dark [windows], Gerry Glynn’s face leered back at me, his hair soaked with gasoline, his face spotted with the blood of his last victim, Phil Dimassi. <br>I pulled the shades. <br>"Patrick," Gerry whispered from the center of my chest, "I’m waiting for you.”</i><br><br>26% ... The Broussard and Poole cop show here is LOL funny! Woot! Especially with cats and bloaters.<br><br>31% ... Literate Lehane, laced with humour:<br><i>“I don’t remember if Bubba had ever messed with Cheese or not, but even if he had, Cheese was smart enough to know that, when it came to warfare, Cheese would be the German army and Bubba the Russian winter. So Cheese stuck to the fronts and battles he knew he could win.”</i><br><br>45% ... Nice character development... Some piercing insights into Patrick's makeup, and how he turns his hatred of his cruel father into a shining self-discipline. <br><i>“The crucial difference between my father and me—I hope—has always been a matter of action. He acted on his anger, whenever and wherever it beset him. His temper ruled him the way alcohol or pride or vanity rules other men. At a very early age, just as the child of an alcoholic swears he’ll never drink, I swore to guard against the advance of the red marble, the cold blood, the tendency toward monotone. Choice, I’ve always believed, is all that separates us from animals. A monkey can’t choose to control his appetite. A man can. My father, at certain hideous moments, was an animal. I refuse to be.”</i><br><br>55% ... The anti-climax of the quarry scenes are confused and drawn out a bit too long. <br><br>61% ... I lived in Boston for ten years, so Lehane’s descriptions and pocket histories of the area make the stories come alive, and texture them in small but important ways. Here he mentions Germantown, a history I never knew. Very nice stuff.<br><br>63% ... one insight into Bubba’s sick world of arms dealing, the 100-round Calico M-110 sub-machine pistol. I look up most of the stuff I’ve never heard of in books. This is a sick little sidetrip into male obscenities . <br><i>“The M-110, at full auto, was capable of unleashing <b>one hundred bullets in roughly fifteen seconds.</b>”</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511963820i/24559806._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>71% ... <b>ADVISORY: Do not read the first 3 paragraphs of chapter 26. You don’t need this. </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ horrific child torture and murder <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> All of this chapter is very hard. It somewhat extends the character of Patrick, and his solid relationship with Angela, but it can be skipped.<br><br>Chapter 27 is very hard, too. <br><br>74% ... Patrick, sounding a lot like Robert B. Parker :<br><i>“I’m a PI, because—I dunno, maybe I’m addicted to the great What Comes Next. Maybe I like tearing down facades. That doesn’t make me a good guy. It just makes me a guy who hates people who hide, pretend to be what they’re not.”</i><br><br>The final 1/4 of the book shows the major twist that we perhaps all knew was coming. It's deftly handled, mostly. The final scenes by the house near the woods would have been heart-wrenching, if only Lehane had been more spare, and with less polarised melodrama from the main characters.<br><br>But the Angela/Patrick twist is truly courageous. If Lehane had ended this the other ways, it would have been cowardice. This ending is painful, and wonderful.<br><br>It also seems to me to be a bit of a setup for book #5, vis a vis Patrick and Angela.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11935343562769098237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_459430985" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/459430985" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/459430985?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer459430985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3534961938166605232">Gone, Baby, Gone by Dennis Lehane is a 1999 Harper publication. <br/><br/>I must make a few confessions up front: <br/><br/>1: I saw the movie version of this title a long time ago and it was so good, I’ve always wanted to read the book, because, of course, the book is always better. <br/><br/>2: I haven’t read as many books by this author as I thought. <br/><br/>3: This is my first foray into the Kenzie & Gennaro series. In fact, I didn’t even know this book was a part of a series, until now.<br/><br/>I make these confessions with shaking hand</span>
  <span id="freeText3534961938166605232" style="display:none">Gone, Baby, Gone by Dennis Lehane is a 1999 Harper publication. <br /><br />I must make a few confessions up front: <br /><br />1: I saw the movie version of this title a long time ago and it was so good, I’ve always wanted to read the book, because, of course, the book is always better. <br /><br />2: I haven’t read as many books by this author as I thought. <br /><br />3: This is my first foray into the Kenzie &amp; Gennaro series. In fact, I didn’t even know this book was a part of a series, until now.<br /><br />I make these confessions with shaking hands since I’m sure my admission is tantamount to religious sacrilege to some folks, but hey, you have to start somewhere. <br /><br />I was immensely curious how the book would differ from the movie, since Hollywood is notorious for taking liberties and on many occasions they flub the whole thing up. But, surprisingly the book and movie matched up, with only a few small differences. <br /><br />All the same, the book was better, as I knew it would be, as it paints a far more detailed and emotional rendition, which had me enthralled, and gave me an even greater respect for this author. <br /><br /><br />When Amanda disappears, her Aunt Beatrice hires the PI team of Patrick Kenzie and Angela Gennaro to find her. <br /><br />The case winds up consuming the couple to the point of obsession, always at the forefront of their lives, until another child goes missing…<br /><br />Well, what can you say? This was one incredible story and one that has sparked some rather heated debate in my household, all of us holding strong feelings on how the situation could have been handled. <br /><br />While there is the obvious black and white answer, there are surely those among you who fall into that gray area, where your mind and logic tells you one thing, while your heart is telling you another. <br /><br />But, no matter which way you slice it, this is one very twisty rollercoaster ride, spotlighting human flaws, and what one does to cope with the world, and how there are never easy answers to many of life’s questions. Sometimes the wrong thing feels like the right thing, in a twisted way that only makes sense when you are living in that moment. Those choices could backfire, or not, depending on the situation, could lead to regret, or no regrets. But, a tangled web has been woven, and good people become unwitting pawns in a convoluted scheme, and a price must be paid, a very high price, as it turns out. <br /><br />This story stayed with me a long time and I still run the details over in mind on occasion, still feel sickened by what happened, and still feel conflicted by the decisions made. <br /><br /> When a novel really grabs you, affects your emotions, plays tricks on your mind, and breaks your heart, leaving a lasting impression, well, that’s what great storytelling is all about, and this author sure knows how to weave a tale. <br /><br /><br />5 stars<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3534961938166605232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1383787217" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1383787217" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1383787217?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780688153328" href="/book/show/1245514.Gone_Baby_Gone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-characters">fave-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=mystery-thriller-horror">mystery-thriller-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1383787217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12965055320042881971"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441548576i/16122273._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
<b>“In the middle of the journey of our life I found myself within a dark woods where the straight way was lost.”</b> - <i>Inferno</i>, Dante</blockquote><br/><b>These books crawl under my skin</b>. I always feel brave and strong <i>while reading them</i> because I seem to stomach everything but oh, look at how dumb you are, Anna. <br/><br/>They <i>linger</i> in me. My nightmares say it all. More than the what or the who or the how, the emotion flourishes deeper, digging into me and breaking my defenses. <br/><br/>These books haunt me - I can't find another word rea</span>
  <span id="freeText12965055320042881971" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441548576i/16122273._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
<b>“In the middle of the journey of our life I found myself within a dark woods where the straight way was lost.”</b> - <i>Inferno</i>, Dante</blockquote><br><b>These books crawl under my skin</b>. I always feel brave and strong <i>while reading them</i> because I seem to stomach everything but oh, look at how dumb you are, Anna. <br><br>They <i>linger</i> in me. My nightmares say it all. More than the what or the who or the how, the emotion flourishes deeper, digging into me and breaking my defenses. <br><br>These books haunt me - I can't find another word really. They haunt me with their sharp and hard take on the world. They feed my pessimism until I stop yelling NO MORE! NO MORE! They turn my stomach inside out. They move me. <i>Scar</i> me.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Well, fine, my life's okay, but the world's still a pile of shit for most people. Even if <i>my</i> world is okay, <i>the</i> world is still a pile of evil shit.' You know?"</b>
</blockquote><br>Their strength lies in the power they hold against my thoughts when I'm not reading. <br><br><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/425123.Gone__Baby__Gone__Kenzie___Gennaro___4_" title="Gone, Baby, Gone (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #4) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone, Baby, Gone</a> deals with child abuse</b>. Start with caution, please. Be warned. As usual, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10289.Dennis_Lehane" title="Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Dennis Lehane</a> will take your heart and squeeze, hard, until the darkness covers every tiny hope you were nurturing. <br><br><b>Who has the right to judge? Society? Individuals?</b> As far as I have <i>my</i> answers - and yes, I quite agree with Patrick on this (not always, though), how flawed our reasoning can be - I know that there's no such thing as a right answer here. There's no such thing as a right <i>choice</i>, but shitty choices all the way. This complexity, always present in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10289.Dennis_Lehane" title="Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Dennis Lehane</a>'s book, is what make them so special in my heart. The world is not as Manichean as some people want us to think, even though it would be easier to deal with it if it was. Humans are selfish animals.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Those who did remember probably shrugged off the chill of her memory, turned their heads down to the sports page or up toward the approaching bus. The world is a terrible place, they thought. Bad things happen every day. My bus is late."</b>
</blockquote><br>Is the ability to forget inherent to the human being? Are we all trying to protect ourselves and those we love on an everyday basis? Maybe. Frankly, I'm not skilled enough to judge the world (who is?), and neither is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10289.Dennis_Lehane" title="Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Dennis Lehane</a> : <b>what he offers us here is a portray of the kaleidoscope that is life, and it's brilliant</b>.<br><br>Favorite, then? Well, this is awkward. This book is probably the favorite of many readers, and I expected that it would be the same for me. However, as you can infer from my 4 stars rating, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/425123.Gone__Baby__Gone__Kenzie___Gennaro___4_" title="Gone, Baby, Gone (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #4) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone, Baby, Gone</a> lost the opportunity to uncrown <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21681.Darkness__Take_My_Hand__Kenzie___Gennaro___2_" title="Darkness, Take My Hand (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #2) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkness, Take My Hand</a>. <br><br>What makes this series so different for me? Definitely Patrick and Angie, the heart of the series, with their sarcastic and badass moves (also, Bubba). In the first half of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/425123.Gone__Baby__Gone__Kenzie___Gennaro___4_" title="Gone, Baby, Gone (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #4) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone, Baby, Gone</a>, <b>it seemed to me that Patrick and Angie were only the shells of themselves.</b><br><br>As a standalone, I can't deny that it was an incredible book through and through, even though I found the first half quite slow. Yet it is not a standalone, but part of a series I LOVE, and during the first 50% I missed Patrick's quick mind and wit. I missed Angie's clever retorts. I've read the first three books in the span of 10 days, and I'm pretty sure I've got their spirit well in mind. They weren't quite there at first in my opinion. Except for Bubba. His parts were my little sunshine (I know, I'm such a psycho). <br><br>This being said, after passing the 60% mark, the characters finally gave me the usual feels and ... I love them. So much. <b>It was painful. It was raw. Again, everything is more complex than it appears at first glance</b> : it's almost ridiculous to see how many times <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10289.Dennis_Lehane" title="Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Dennis Lehane</a> can surprise me. Damn. If I wasn't so engrossed in his stories, I'd be mad. <br><br>But now? <b>I'm pretty sure I'm broken.</b><br><br><b>Ps.</b> I said earlier that I would wait before starting the fifth book and as it is... <i>I can't</i>. I need more Bubba, more Patrick, and more Angie. Now even more. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="12965055320042881971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer948483471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1324883748790243564">I <em>just</em> finished this book- like, literally, turned the final page, put it down, and am now writing. So, it's possible that I'm violating some rule of thumb akin to waiting two hours after you eat before swimming or not going to bed angry. However, there's a sort of queasy discomfort I have after finishing this fourth volume of the Kenzie & Gennaro corpus that might dissolve given enough lag time that I wanted to get down.<br/> <br/>Lehane has left me with the disquieting malaise of a <em>
  <strong>wicked problem</strong>
</em>. W</span>
  <span id="freeText1324883748790243564" style="display:none">I <em>just</em> finished this book- like, literally, turned the final page, put it down, and am now writing. So, it's possible that I'm violating some rule of thumb akin to waiting two hours after you eat before swimming or not going to bed angry. However, there's a sort of queasy discomfort I have after finishing this fourth volume of the Kenzie &amp; Gennaro corpus that might dissolve given enough lag time that I wanted to get down.<br /> <br />Lehane has left me with the disquieting malaise of a <em>
  <strong>wicked problem</strong>
</em>. Wicked problems are defined (in part) by their lack of definitive solution. And, at least for me, uncertainty is not a favorite feeling. This book, of course, is not a discourse in moral philosophy. Patrick and Angie are brought in to look for the missing child of a less than stellar mother at the behest of the girl's uncle. As usual, there are layers of intrigue, action and tension for miles. <br /> <br />If nothing more, this one will definitely make you <em>feel</em> something, but it will likely be a something you can't quite pin down. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1324883748790243564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1397722792" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1397722792" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1397722792?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=epic-reads-for-light-and-dark-pup">epic-reads-for-light-and-dark-pup</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=in-the-minority-on-this-one">in-the-minority-on-this-one</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1397722792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10627245796730502835"><br/>*4.5 stars* <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Love like that? Hell. It seems so pure, it's damn near criminal.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Soooo....I've missed my Angie and Patrick, I'm not guna lie. So when I got the empty feelings one usually gets after finishing a fantastic book and not knowing what to read, I started to get <b>an ache that couldn't be filled</b> by anything other than a beautifully flawed and tortured detective and his snarky partner in crime. See, there are only 6 books and I decided to break them up so I didn't lose them all at o</span>
  <span id="freeText10627245796730502835" style="display:none"><br>*4.5 stars* <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Love like that? Hell. It seems so pure, it's damn near criminal.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Soooo....I've missed my Angie and Patrick, I'm not guna lie. So when I got the empty feelings one usually gets after finishing a fantastic book and not knowing what to read, I started to get <b>an ache that couldn't be filled</b> by anything other than a beautifully flawed and tortured detective and his snarky partner in crime. See, there are only 6 books and I decided to break them up so I didn't lose them all at once....I'm so happy I did this now.<br><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>The silence of the dead says, Goodbye.<br>The silence of the missing says, Find me.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_inline_nhs9ch0BCm1ss3rei_zpsksro6mrd.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444141814ra/16458802.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_inline_nhs9ch0BCm1ss3rei_zpsksro6mrd.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>I don't know what I could say that hasn't already been said on my part, but I feel like this story deserves a review, ya know? It feels wrong that I wouldn't give voice to one of my new favorite series that I occupy a lot of time daydreaming about. But, in many ways, it's hard to review multiple stories pertaining to one series, and even harder when you hit one in the series that just....isn't as good. Now, the funny thing here?? <b>This book was still excellent</b>. We still had my wonderful Patrick, asshole Angie (sorry, but she is a total snark-monster (which I love)), Bubba, and a deep mystery that keeps you enthralled until the final page...but I just didn't <i>feel</i> during the mystery.<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>We were slippery creatures, our impulses ruled by a variety of forces, many of them incomprehensible even to ourselves.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/15657767_zpsw4slqflf.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444141814ra/16458803.gif" alt=" photo 15657767_zpsw4slqflf.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Maybe that makes me a monster, maybe I am, indeed, in the minority on this one, and maybe I should have loved this way more than I did. But after the excellence of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21681.Darkness__Take_My_Hand__Kenzie___Gennaro___2_" title="Darkness, Take My Hand (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #2) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkness, Take My Hand</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/425124.Sacred__Kenzie___Gennaro___3_" title="Sacred (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #3) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Sacred</a>, <b>this story fell flat for me</b>. Less action, less investment on my part, and just a lack of depth I'm so very used to with these mysteries. Now, when I say I didn't <i>feel</i> as much, I mean I didn't have any leads as to who it was, I didn't really freak out when something would happen (aside from that horrid house scene which was just.....nightmare inducing...) and I just...wanted a serial killer story or a deceptive siren woman to come back so I could be engrossed in a different way. All in all? I didn't like the story line. Awesome ending...but the mystery fell flat for me, which is the total opposite of everyone on GR, it seems. <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>I moved over and she sat beside me. She took my face in her hands, but I couldn't meet her eyes, was sure that seeing the warmth and the love in them would make me feel more soiled, for some reason, more unhinged.<br>She kissed my forehead and then my eyelids, the tears drying on my face, brought my head down to her shoulder, and kissed the back of my neck.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>Patrick, despite the gravity of this case, is in a good place. He's happy...he's with the girl he's been in love with since he was a kid and they are happily living with one another. But, and this is a big but (hehe), they have been through hell and back..and it shows. They only take little cases and they avoid matters like this. It's not good for them-it weighs heavily on their minds and souls, and they've seen enough darkness to last them a lifetime. <b>They just want to be happy</b>. But what happens when a desperate Aunt won't take no for an answer. What happens when the issue at hand hits you right in the gut..what happens when taking this case <b>might lead to the ultimate sacrifice of your happiness</b>?<br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_nlml2mAk5V1uqz4z7o1_400_zpshq0mtb6b.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444141242ra/16458774.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_nlml2mAk5V1uqz4z7o1_400_zpshq0mtb6b.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I don't know what to say," she whispered.<br>"Nothing to say." I cleared my throat, wrapped my arms around her abdomen and lower back. I could hear her heart beating. She felt so good, so beautiful, so everything that was right in the world. And I still felt like dying."</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>I feel for them...I really do. Because I could <i>never</i> turn down that case. Ever. So, anyway. I don't think there's a whole lot more to say. It's simple: <b>This series is epic</b>, the stories draw you in no matter the content, even if it's not your favorite, and the characters leave you aching for them and desperate for more. I'm sad, really, I have to wait so long in between so I can find that ultimate enjoyment...but it's for my own good and....sigh...fine...I <u>will</u> be strong. <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>At the end of an April day, after the sun has descended but before night has fallen, the city turns a hushed, unsettled gray. Another day has died, always more quickly than expected. Muted yellow or orange lights appear in window squares and shaft from car grilles, and the coming dark promises a deepening chill.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><br><br><br>For more of my reviews, please visit:<br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="Twitter" href="https://twitter.com/starcrossedblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660580.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="RSS" href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/starcrossedbookblog/METU" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660581.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="BLOGLOVIN" href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/star-crossed-book-blog-13035961" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660579.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br><br><br>**************************<br><br><br>I figured it would be fun to list my favorites in order until I find time to write a review:<br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21681.Darkness__Take_My_Hand__Kenzie___Gennaro___2_" title="Darkness, Take My Hand (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #2) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkness, Take My Hand</a>
  <br>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/425124.Sacred__Kenzie___Gennaro___3_" title="Sacred (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #3) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Sacred</a>
  <br>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/425123.Gone__Baby__Gone__Kenzie___Gennaro___4_" title="Gone, Baby, Gone (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #4) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone, Baby, Gone</a>
  <br>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21685.A_Drink_Before_the_War__Kenzie___Gennaro___1_" title="A Drink Before the War (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #1) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">A Drink Before the War</a>
</b><br><br>It might come as a shock to y'all that this book is one of my least favorites...well, <b>the story just didn't compare</b>.<br><br>Review to come.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10627245796730502835" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
