<div id="review_135613309" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135613309" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4677640-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472613597p2/4677640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135613309?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/4677640-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061336218" href="/book/show/16973.Gone_Baby_Gone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4677640-richard?shelf=dicks">dicks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4677640-richard?shelf=author-lehane">author-lehane</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4677640-richard?shelf=re-read-list">re-read-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4677640-richard?shelf=great-endings">great-endings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4677640-richard?shelf=urban-gothic">urban-gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4677640-richard?shelf=essential-crime">essential-crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135613309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12550394944758663956"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“When I was young, I asked my priest how to get to heaven and still protect yourself from all the evil in the world. He told me what God told His children; 'You are sheep among wolves, be wise as the serpent, yet innocent as doves.'”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>This is by far the best installment in Dennis Lehane's great series following inner city Boston private detectives Patrick Kenzie and Angela Gennaro (with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21681.Darkness__Take_My_Hand__Kenzie___Gennaro___2_' title='Darkness, Take My Hand (Kenzie & Gennaro, #2) by Dennis Lehane' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darkness, Take My Hand</a> being a close second). And the VERY BEST detective novel I've read so far. I </span>
  <span id="freeText12550394944758663956" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“When I was young, I asked my priest how to get to heaven and still protect yourself from all the evil in the world. He told me what God told His children; 'You are sheep among wolves, be wise as the serpent, yet innocent as doves.'”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>This is by far the best installment in Dennis Lehane's great series following inner city Boston private detectives Patrick Kenzie and Angela Gennaro (with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21681.Darkness__Take_My_Hand__Kenzie___Gennaro___2_" title="Darkness, Take My Hand (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #2) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkness, Take My Hand</a> being a close second). And the VERY BEST detective novel I've read so far. I know that's saying a lot but I don't say it lightly. Lehane always proves to be a master of plotting, and here, he not only takes a simple missing child mystery and turns it into something endlessly addictive and compelling, but he ends it well too. The final reveal and resolution came at me like a hard fist to the face, sending me reeling for days. It's ingenious and truly one of a kind, and left me to ponder even my own morality. When a novel in such a crowded and cliché-ridden field as the detective genre can leave you so affected, that book is truly something special. There are so many great moments in this book; the plot develops at a flawless pace, and every character is pitch-perfect and memorable. And I love the way the Patrick and Angie get so involved that the case affects them personally, taking over their lives, challenging everything they believe in. All of this helps to rank this book as one of the best novels in modern crime fiction, right up there on my list with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135716000?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Clockers</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135614588?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A Simple Plan</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165628062?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The 25th Hour</a>, and the author's other masterwork, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21671.Mystic_River" title="Mystic River by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Mystic River</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12550394944758663956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1985964819" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8148738231042019799"><b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18856368-september-2017-group-read-gone-baby-gone-by-dennis-lehane' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mystery, Crime & Thriller - Sept. 2017 Group Read<br/></a>

They say Helene(Amanda's mom) leaves her alone almost every night - "Gone, Baby, Gone". Lt.Jack Doyle says his Boston Police detectives are enough help.<br/><br/>Patrick/Angie & Det.Remy begin search. Lionel tells them he heard Helene & "Skinny" Ray talk about a N</span>

  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18856368-september-2017-group-read-gone-baby-gone-by-dennis-lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Mystery, Crime &amp; Thriller - Sept. 2017 Group Read<br></a>

</blockquote><br>Aunt Beatrice &amp; Uncle Lionel hire Patrick Kenzie &amp; Angie Gennaro to find their niece Amanda(4). They say Helene(Amanda's mom) leaves her alone almost every night - "Gone, Baby, Gone". Lt.Jack Doyle says his Boston Police detectives are enough help.<br><br>Patrick/Angie &amp; Det.Remy begin search. Lionel tells them he heard Helene &amp; "Skinny" Ray talk about a NH $200,000 "Drug" money run for "Chesse" Olamon. Helene says she saw Kimmie/WeeDavid were together on the "kidnap" night. They are found dead with a note "Gtwo hundred + composure = child". <br><br>"Cheese" wants his money back. Money is found behind Kimmie/WeeDavid's. A failed setup with "Cheese" at a Quarry for the money/Amanda swap fails - 2 people killed. Money &amp; Amanda not found, she is now pronounced dead. Jack Doyle resigned running a department dedicated to children.<br><br>The ending could have been better. Det.Remy, Lionel &amp; Doyle wanted a better life for Amanda. Did a "kidnap" setup get them $200,000 to split &amp; Amanda a better life? Or Amanda may just be returned and money lost?!</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6610423-gone-baby-gone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=detective-books">detective-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1645499951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16705738175540277549">Patrick and Angie have led rough careers as private investigators and after the events in Sacred, they’ve decided to pull back a little. When we catch up with them in Gone Baby Gone, they’ve all but sworn off cases that could lead to violence, death and destruction. Unfortunately for them, when young Amanda McCready goes missing, Amanda’s grieving Aunt and Uncle are persistent in their requests for the detectives’ help.<br/><br/>Patrick and Angie aren’t sure they’ll be able to offer much up in the way of </span>
  <span id="freeText16705738175540277549" style="display:none">Patrick and Angie have led rough careers as private investigators and after the events in Sacred, they’ve decided to pull back a little. When we catch up with them in Gone Baby Gone, they’ve all but sworn off cases that could lead to violence, death and destruction. Unfortunately for them, when young Amanda McCready goes missing, Amanda’s grieving Aunt and Uncle are persistent in their requests for the detectives’ help.<br /><br />Patrick and Angie aren’t sure they’ll be able to offer much up in the way of help. The Boston PD have been working around the clock trying to find Amanda and with her face plastered all over the city, every citizen will have their eyes peeled. There’s also the matter of the girl’s mother, Helene. To put it simply, she’s a burnout. She spends all her time glued to the TV, strung-out on drugs and alcohol. In fact, her negligence was the direct cause of Amanda’s disappearance. Patrick and Angie team up with Crimes Against Children (CAC) officials Remy Broussard and Nick Poole. The foursome work together to turn Boston upside down.<br /><br />If you thought Darkness, Take My Hand was a tough read, Gone Baby Gone will rip your heart out. Patrick and Angie are put through the proverbial thresher, their lives and relationships come under unbelievable strain as they desperately try to recover the missing girl. While the body count isn’t on the level of the first few novels, the tension is tight and unrelenting.<br /><br />If anything, Lehane can write a hell of a page-turner. Gone Baby Gone is a visceral read that I wouldn’t recommend for those with a weak stomach or who deal well with child abuse in fiction. But I would argue it’s an important read, if only that it questions morality and what it means to “do the right thing”.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16705738175540277549" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_604336034" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/604336034" />
    <a title="Anushka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8377084-anushka"><img alt="Anushka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452007230p2/8377084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/604336034?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anushka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anushka" href="/user/show/8377084-anushka">Anushka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061336218" href="/book/show/16973.Gone_Baby_Gone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=liked-it">liked-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=i-cried">i-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=them-feels">them-feels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=mindfuck">mindfuck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=worth-the-hype">worth-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=suspense-thriller-horror">suspense-thriller-horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer604336034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10004605496944618637">First time. It’s the first time a thriller has made me cry.<br/><br/>I mean, you don’t shed tears while reading these books, you read one then you read another one. But not this one. No, this one is going to <i>haunt</i> me for a long time, like all Dennis Lehane books do. I still think about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21671.Mystic_River' title='Mystic River by Dennis Lehane' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mystic River</a> and feel a chill run down my spine.<br/><br/><i>Gone, Baby, Gone</i> dealt with some very sensitive issues wrapped in a blanket of controversial subjects. Kidnapping is a topic that is bound to make you emotionally invested but</span>
  <span id="freeText10004605496944618637" style="display:none">First time. It’s the first time a thriller has made me cry.<br /><br />I mean, you don’t shed tears while reading these books, you read one then you read another one. But not this one. No, this one is going to <i>haunt</i> me for a long time, like all Dennis Lehane books do. I still think about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21671.Mystic_River" title="Mystic River by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Mystic River</a> and feel a chill run down my spine.<br /><br /><i>Gone, Baby, Gone</i> dealt with some very sensitive issues wrapped in a blanket of controversial subjects. Kidnapping is a topic that is bound to make you emotionally invested but in no book I’ve ever read, it was done with such explicitness. All the gory details were mentioned for which I took about 5 to 10 seconds to digest and move forward. This book repeatedly tests the grey area of what’s legal and what’s moral, <b>what you are <i>supposed</i> to do and what you <i>should</i> do</b>.<br /><br />It is a well-plotted mystery with various number of plot twists that leads up to a galvanizing climax but the other part of the story comes back to stare at your face again and again. <b>What is right and what is wrong and who gets to decide that, who is the better judge of all things good or bad in this world.</b><br /> <br />Extremely thought provoking, emotionally stimulating with all the characteristics of a good thriller, this book deserves <b>5 stars</b> without putting any thought. <br /><br />In the end, I hope the incidents mentioned here were all fictitious, please do not tell me that this happens in real life to little kids but that is the whole point of this book. Still, I pray that no one goes through this trauma in their lives, it is unfair and no one deserves this!<br /><br />Recommended to all. <br />Now I’m off to watch the movie, which I’ve heard it’s as good as the book and order some more books by Lehane.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10004605496944618637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17529407430764976961"><br/>3.5<br/><br/>I think I had my hopes up too high on this one. I've become a Lehane fan and I have heard a lot of great opinions on this novel, so I went in with great anticipation. Obviously, I'm not saying the book was bad, I gave it a 3.5 rounded up to 4, but it just didn't wow me as I had expected. I was looking for something entertaining along the lines of Mystic River, and in my opinion there was no comparison. <br/><br/>I thought the opening was strong in this 'Kenzie & Gennaro' segment, and there was plenty o</span>
  <span id="freeText17529407430764976961" style="display:none"><br />3.5<br /><br />I think I had my hopes up too high on this one. I've become a Lehane fan and I have heard a lot of great opinions on this novel, so I went in with great anticipation. Obviously, I'm not saying the book was bad, I gave it a 3.5 rounded up to 4, but it just didn't wow me as I had expected. I was looking for something entertaining along the lines of Mystic River, and in my opinion there was no comparison. <br /><br />I thought the opening was strong in this 'Kenzie &amp; Gennaro' segment, and there was plenty of action and hard-edge scenarios to keep me turning pages in this crime/thriller, but there were too many strands in the web that held this plot together. I felt there were too many twists and turns threaded in the story. I couldn't buy it. <br /><br />For those like me who are way behind the curve in this series, let me just give you this warning if you are thinking about wading in; there are some brutal details in these pages involving children. Some of the descriptions are pretty graphic, so be careful if you are the kind that lacks the stomach for this kind of reading. <br /><br />And lastly, I won't spoil anything, but I will just say that I thought the ending left what might be an interesting debate on what might have been the right course of action. Who was right, Kenzie, or Gennaro? Some great points from each side, but one thing this novel brought to life is sure; there is a cancer in our society involving, not just abused, but neglected children as well. A person has to get a license to drive, a license to get married, hell, they even need a license to catch a fish, but any lowlife scumbag can bring a child into this world. So, how do you we combat this? Anyway, I'll keep from going off on a tangent on that subject, but it does play a main role in the plot of this story. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11280173462511211766">WOW...what I ride Lehane takes the reader on through the seedy side of Boston. The heroes are not really good guys and the bad guys are really, really bad. Two PI's take on the case of a missing child, and find themselves in the middle of corruption, mob activity, drug dealers, psycho's and everything in between. This is a brutal story where nothing is black and white. Trying not to cross the line is a struggle and nothing or no one is as it or they appear.<br/><br/> When I read this I knew how much I lik</span>
  <span id="freeText11280173462511211766" style="display:none">WOW...what I ride Lehane takes the reader on through the seedy side of Boston. The heroes are not really good guys and the bad guys are really, really bad. Two PI's take on the case of a missing child, and find themselves in the middle of corruption, mob activity, drug dealers, psycho's and everything in between. This is a brutal story where nothing is black and white. Trying not to cross the line is a struggle and nothing or no one is as it or they appear.<br /><br /> When I read this I knew how much I liked "Mystic River" but I had forgotten how gritty and uncomfortable that book was.....but this book brought all of that back to me. I did not know that this was part of a series, and being the fourth one I wish I had started at the beginning, though the story did not lose anything....except maybe in reference to some of the characters past. <br /><br /> Once I catch my breath and quit shuddering I may start with book one! This is not for the weak stomached nor faint of heart. But for fans of hard hitting crime/suspense with steely characters this is the way to go.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10873607189279498214">I've determined that pretty much every mystery/suspense/thriller/whatever book I read is going to land at three stars. It takes a lot for these books to break through into the four star range, and I don't think any of them are ever five star caliber. <br/><br/>Lehane, Coben, Grisham, most King, Connelly, etc. They're all fine authors, but all of them have a limit to how great they can be, and they all settle for a decent story that is enthralling at times but ultimately forgettable. <br/><br/>This story was just wh</span>
  <span id="freeText10873607189279498214" style="display:none">I've determined that pretty much every mystery/suspense/thriller/whatever book I read is going to land at three stars. It takes a lot for these books to break through into the four star range, and I don't think any of them are ever five star caliber. <br /><br />Lehane, Coben, Grisham, most King, Connelly, etc. They're all fine authors, but all of them have a limit to how great they can be, and they all settle for a decent story that is enthralling at times but ultimately forgettable. <br /><br />This story was just what I expected. I enjoyed it, but it didn't stick with me or impact me at all beyond just providing a mildly entertaining story. <br /><br />It may be time to leave this genre alone for a minute.</span>

<div id="review_1183341081" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1183341081" />
    <a title="Rade " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8187431-rade"><img alt="Rade " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426096920p2/8187431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1183341081?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rade " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rade " href="/user/show/8187431-rade">Rade </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8187431-rade?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1183341081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7460321562118393130">I have just one more Kenzie & Gennaro book to read. Each one of the books I've highly enjoyed and would recommend them to everyone. <br/><br/>This one is no exception. What I like about Lehane's books is not only his fantastic writing but also his ability to make a simple promise of a book into something that is hard to put down. This one started with a missing child and went out of control, spiralling into a world of drugs, money, corruption, and the want for fame and glory. <br/><br/>Most of the characters in the</span>
  <span id="freeText7460321562118393130" style="display:none">I have just one more Kenzie &amp; Gennaro book to read. Each one of the books I've highly enjoyed and would recommend them to everyone. <br /><br />This one is no exception. What I like about Lehane's books is not only his fantastic writing but also his ability to make a simple promise of a book into something that is hard to put down. This one started with a missing child and went out of control, spiralling into a world of drugs, money, corruption, and the want for fame and glory. <br /><br />Most of the characters in the book are likable, even those who are horrible human beings. The dialogue is always smooth, revealing bits of important information with each chapter. The last chapter was hard to read. You know there are people out there who do horrible things and you know you might even know some who are straight criminals, but it still does not prepare you for ultimate reveal. It makes you question whether a criminal can turn his life around and become a good person, the kind that even someone in the law enforcement would not question. it also makes you question whether a criminal can change into a person who cares about those around him. Lehane has a way with his story where there are no points where you would stop and say, "well that's a big coincidence. He's just using that because he does not know how to connect the dots without being cliche." <br /><br />I highly recommend Lehane's books. Over the years I've become one of his big fans. He is a great author and from interviews he seems like an overall great guy. I hope after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7853757.Moonlight_Mile__Kenzie___Gennaro__6_" title="Moonlight Mile (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro,#6) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Moonlight Mile</a> he does more of Kenzie and Gennaro books. I really like them and I hope he at least mentions them in some other books, just for shits and giggles. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7460321562118393130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12949855-corey?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12949855-corey?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer779094847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3331655940579120768">Gone Baby Gone is a great who-done-it story, but also very true to life, because the events that took place in this book could happen to anybody!<br/><br/>Gone Baby Gone is about 2 Boston Private Investigators Patrick Kenzie and Angela Gennaro, who are approached by the Aunt of 4 year old girl Amanda McCready, who had disappeared without a trace, and whose Mother is heavy into drugs and alcohol. Kenzie and Gennaro accept the case and set out to solve the dark mystery behind Amanda's disappearance.<br/><br/>I do kno</span>
  <span id="freeText3331655940579120768" style="display:none">Gone Baby Gone is a great who-done-it story, but also very true to life, because the events that took place in this book could happen to anybody!<br><br>Gone Baby Gone is about 2 Boston Private Investigators Patrick Kenzie and Angela Gennaro, who are approached by the Aunt of 4 year old girl Amanda McCready, who had disappeared without a trace, and whose Mother is heavy into drugs and alcohol. Kenzie and Gennaro accept the case and set out to solve the dark mystery behind Amanda's disappearance.<br><br>I do know that Gone Baby Gone is part of a series, book #4, I've read the first book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21685.A_Drink_Before_the_War__Kenzie___Gennaro___1_" title="A Drink Before the War (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #1) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1386921356s/21685.jpg" alt="A Drink Before the War (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #1) by Dennis Lehane" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>, which got me acquainted with Kenzie and Gennaro, I have yet to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21681.Darkness__Take_My_Hand__Kenzie___Gennaro___2_" title="Darkness, Take My Hand (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #2) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1392049150s/21681.jpg" alt="Darkness, Take My Hand (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #2) by Dennis Lehane" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/425124.Sacred__Kenzie___Gennaro___3_" title="Sacred (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #3) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1435786018s/425124.jpg" alt="Sacred (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #3) by Dennis Lehane" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>. The reason I wanted to jump right into Gone Baby Gone is because I own the movie, which was directed by Ben Affleck, and stars his younger brother Casey Affleck, which was one of his first big starring roles, and I loved the movie where I'm a die-hard fan of both Ben and Casey! And co-stars are Morgan Freeman, Ed Harris, and Michelle Monaghan. The book follows the movie about like 90%, with like 10% difference! But I recommend reading the book first.<br><br>I love Lehane's writing style, the story is written in the 1st person, and with the dialogue you feel like you're in the story, you're like right there experiencing it! <br><br>A phenomenal story, great plot, and just when you think you've found out what's going on, it all goes in a totally different direction, you'll never see it coming! If you've never read this book, I just have one thing to say, once you read it you'll never regret it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3331655940579120768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_379872230" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/379872230" />
    <a title="Harry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7597429-harry"><img alt="Harry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380595404p2/7597429.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/379872230?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Harry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Harry" href="/user/show/7597429-harry">Harry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7597429-harry?shelf=detective-mystery">detective-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7597429-harry?shelf=noir-detective-series">noir-detective-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7597429-harry?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer379872230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15413006561060905790">Hmmmm...someone liked one of my reviews and I checked out this person's reading list as well as their reviews and heard mention somewhere in there a sentence or two about heroes, one likeable, the other...well, more along the lines of a sociopath. Dennis Lehane, among other authors was mentioned in this respect.<br/><br/>As always, my curiosity was piqued, and although I checked out the other named authors I did finally settle on Dennis Lehane. It was a good decision. Perhaps one of the best reading decis</span>
  <span id="freeText15413006561060905790" style="display:none">Hmmmm...someone liked one of my reviews and I checked out this person's reading list as well as their reviews and heard mention somewhere in there a sentence or two about heroes, one likeable, the other...well, more along the lines of a sociopath. Dennis Lehane, among other authors was mentioned in this respect.<br /><br />As always, my curiosity was piqued, and although I checked out the other named authors I did finally settle on Dennis Lehane. It was a good decision. Perhaps one of the best reading decisions ever. Lehane's Kenzie and Gennaro series is best described as being in the Noir series of detectives (I am reminded of Andrew Vacchs as another excellent member of this genre). This study of the darker side of humanity is epxressed through very witty and sometimes humerous dialogue that contrasts sharply with each novel's antagonists: awash in horrendous and pure evil. Lehane's descriptions are on the mark, there's no guessing as you attempt to imagine each scene described: you see it as it was meant to be seen. I've seen other novelists (Katherine Slaughter, for example) try to pull this off but frankly, the writing does not compare in both dialogue and descriptions. At least, not after you've read Lehane.<br /><br />As my other reviews attest, I'm interested in the lone hero in novels (series only, please), an interest awakened by the Jack Reacher novels of Lee Child and Coben's Myron Bolitar series as well as other excellent novelists (see my other reviews). In the Reacher novels, all aspects of the hero (consistent values, propensity for violence, temptation, etc.) are encased in a single hero: Jack Reacher. Harlan Coben splits these characteristics and infuses them into two heroes: Myron Bolitar (values and principles), and Win (our favorite sociopath). Lehane takes this a step further and presents us with a three way split from Jack Reacher: Gennaro (the good), Kenzie (the good mixed with propensity for violence), and Bubba (our favorite sociopath).<br /><br />When it comes to Noir, you can't get any better than Dennis Lehane. And if you're interested in this genre, do take the time to read the works of Andrew Vacchs (start at the beginning folks!). Outstanding in their own right and as good, if not better than Lehane's Kenzie and Gennaro series.<br /><br />If you've read this review of the Kenzie and Gennaro books, than you've read them all. His work will keep you up late into the night, reading, when you should be sleeping and getting ready for work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15413006561060905790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane Stewart" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart">Jane Stewart</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer661856790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17219326250451552792">Wonderful writing, but the subject matter and ending were depressing and dark.<br/><br/>I’ve read three Lehane books. All three of them have horrible things happening to children: a father prostituting his son, pedophiles kidnaping and torturing children, drug addicted mothers ignoring and neglecting children. This book has pedophiles torturing children and disgustingly neglectful mothers.<br/><br/>The mystery was solved, but the end was depressing. The novel is about injustice, the poor, drug users, race and simil</span>
  <span id="freeText17219326250451552792" style="display:none">Wonderful writing, but the subject matter and ending were depressing and dark.<br /><br />I’ve read three Lehane books. All three of them have horrible things happening to children: a father prostituting his son, pedophiles kidnaping and torturing children, drug addicted mothers ignoring and neglecting children. This book has pedophiles torturing children and disgustingly neglectful mothers.<br /><br />The mystery was solved, but the end was depressing. The novel is about injustice, the poor, drug users, race and similar problems.<br /><br />I love Lehane’s writing - the way he describes scenes, people, clothes, emotions, smells, - and his dialogue. I feel like I’m living it. It’s very full writing. I’d probably give it 5 stars if it had a more fulfilling ending.<br /><br />Patrick and Angie investigate the kidnaping of a little girl with complications along the way. This is intricately plotted - twists and turns I didn’t expect. Bubba is my favorite character. I would have liked a larger role for him, but the story was about other things and was good.<br /><br />The narrator Jonathan Davis was excellent.<br /><br />DATA:<br />Narrative mode: 1st person Patrick. Unabridged audiobook length: 13 hrs and 35 mins. Swearing language: strong but rarely used. Sexual language: none. Number of sex scenes: 2 told not shown. Setting: around 1998 Boston, Massachusetts. Book copyright: 1998. Genre: crime mystery suspense.</span>

<div id="review_8568237" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8568237" />
    <a title="Luis Roman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/558664-luis-roman"><img alt="Luis Roman" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8568237?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luis Roman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luis Roman" href="/user/show/558664-luis-roman">Luis Roman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061374197" href="/book/show/1245520.Gone_Baby_Gone">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">mystery lovers</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8568237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4464038794151126925"> Sad, sad, sad. this is the Boston of Dennis Lehane, populated by tough guys, lost souls, and heartbreak. This is the Boston of Patrick Kenzie, flawed hero of several previous Lehane novels. This is the first Lehane novel I read, and I found it compelling, if not enjoyable. The crime is not as important here, as the way the people around it react. Kenzie's primary character trait is his nobility - it compels to continue investigating the crime, even though he has several opportunites, and even m</span>
  <span id="freeText4464038794151126925" style="display:none"> Sad, sad, sad. this is the Boston of Dennis Lehane, populated by tough guys, lost souls, and heartbreak. This is the Boston of Patrick Kenzie, flawed hero of several previous Lehane novels. This is the first Lehane novel I read, and I found it compelling, if not enjoyable. The crime is not as important here, as the way the people around it react. Kenzie's primary character trait is his nobility - it compels to continue investigating the crime, even though he has several opportunites, and even more reasons, to drop it. Ultimately his nobility forces to make a choice which costs him the only thing in the world he truly loves.<br /> Lehane seeks to question fundamental notions of right and wrong, and he does it in a profoundly disturbing fashion. Is parenthood a right, or a privilege? Who has the right to determine the answer to that question? When does justice require a person to step outside the law? How much would you be willing to give up to maintain your own sense of honor?<br /> I don't know if I am completely hooked by Lehane, but I will definitely pick up his next book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4464038794151126925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HsNuKNReIzxhQdRgYQgb5vZEF9f916pRUqjCQ9cGg6AAdIktnV/ehnE7nxB/fNG2GaEQ1otBBmffLf9gzOek7Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

After losing her job when the Garmin factory shuts down, Nonie is left with major money issues—as in, she has none. Desperate, she has to turn to the one place she’s avoided working since dropping out of college--her family’s funeral home.It wasn’t that Nonie feared the dead. In fact the opposite was true. She sees them—literally, and had been seeing the dead ever since she can remember. She tried telling her parents about it when she was a child, but they’d vehemently dismissed it to imaginary friends, so she’d stopped talking about it. There were only two people who actually knew Nonie’s secret and knew she was the real deal. One was Buggy Mouton, her best friend since kindergarten, and the other was Guy Skinard, whom Nonie considered her one true love since the day she’d laid eyes on him in high school. Buggy now worked at MeeMaw’s Café off of Main in Clay Point, and Guy, as usual, remained ever at her side—the only difference being he’d died in a freak boating accident nine years ago. Still the prankster even in death, Guy loved causing chaos, especially with men Nonie occasionally dated. She could only imagine what mayhem he might stir up while mirroring her at the funeral home and mingling with the newly departed.Only hours into the first day of her new job, pandemonium engulfs the funeral home, and much to Nonie’s surprise, it has nothing to do with Guy. It’s brought on by the family they’re serving. Seventy-two–year-old Dover Fontenot, the Major of Clay Point, dies in a car accident after indulging in a little extra-curricular activity—only the activity wasn’t with his wife , Hazel. And when Dover’s mistress, Anna Mae Turner, shows up at the funeral home for the visitation hell’s gates rip open and Broussard’s Funeral Home suddenly turns into a geriatric war zone.Amidst the flying hairpieces, canes and curses, Nonie’s best friend, Buggy, decides to drop by the funeral home with news she can’t wait to share. A cable network in New Orleans wants to put together a paranormal investigation team and have them check out purported haunted locations in Louisiana. For every location with solid filming potential, each member of the team gets a five hundred dollar pay check. And Buggy knows without question that if anyone can sniff out the ‘restless’ dead, it’s Nonie.Knowing nothing about paranormal investigation, but lured by the sound of the adventure and the dollar signs circling through her head, Nonie agrees to become part of the Boo Krewe, the name Buggy has formally given the makeshift team.The lure of money may be one thing, but what Nonie doesn’t realize is that occasionally the dead, so excited that someone can actually see and hear them, decide to follow her home, into her bed—the bathroom—the shower. And adding to this new-found frustration, Nonie barely finishes her first investigation when she gets a visit from Anna Mae Turner—the mayor’s former mistress—now dead, as well, and harassingly insistent that Nonie bring her killer to light.Nonie quickly learns that the ‘gift’ she’s carried since birth is really a giant wart on the butt of life—and no amount of Compound W is going to make it <span id="freeTextContainer16183145946743488952">Dennis Lehane (born Aug 4th, 1966) is an American author. He has written several novels, including the New York Times bestseller Mystic River, which was later made into an Academy Award winning film, also called Mystic River, directed by Clint Eastwood and starring Sean Penn, Tim Robbins, and Kevin Bacon (Lehane can be briefly seen waving from a car in the parade scene at the end of the film). The</span>
  <span id="freeText16183145946743488952" style="display:none">Dennis Lehane (born Aug 4th, 1966) is an American author. He has written several novels, including the New York Times bestseller Mystic River, which was later made into an Academy Award winning film, also called Mystic River, directed by Clint Eastwood and starring Sean Penn, Tim Robbins, and Kevin Bacon (Lehane can be briefly seen waving from a car in the parade scene at the end of the film). The novel was a finalist for the PEN/Winship Award and won the Anthony Award and the Barry Award for Best Novel, the Massachusetts Book Award in Fiction, and France's Prix Mystere de la Critique.<br /><br /></span>

A stellar student, brilliant but aloof, she seemed destined to escape her upbringing. Yet Amanda\'s aunt is once more knocking on Patrick Kenzie\'s door, fearing the worst for the little girl who has blossomed into a striking, clever young woman—a woman who hasn\'t been seen in weeks.Haunted by their consciences, Kenzie and Gennaro revisit the case that troubled them the most. Their search leads them into a world of identity thieves, methamphetamine dealers, a mentally unstable crime boss and his equally demented wife, a priceless, thousand-year-old cross, and a happily homicidal Russian gangster. It\'s a world in which motives and allegiances constantly shift and mistakes are fatal.In their desperate fight to confront the past and find Amanda McCready, Kenzie and Gennaro will be forced to question if it\'s possible to do the wrong thing and still be right or to do the right thing and still be wrong.
